Preserving that history is a responsibility we all share. Bridge, a house DJ and preservationist, leads an interactive exploration of where this music came from and the responsibility we carry to maintain its history."}

North London outfit Ivy Lab were brought together out of a shared enthusiasm for experimentations on the fringes of the UK bass music scene. Minted in late 2015, and borrowing the same raison d'\u00eatre as its elder sibling nightlife brand; 20/20 LDN Recordings was unveiled with the pseudo-mixtape/compilation LP \u2018Ivy Lab presents 20/20 Volume.1\u2019 - described as \u201cuncompromising, insightful and rather awesome : 9/10\u201d (Mixmag) and \u201cimpossible to categorise : 9/10\u201d (DJ Mag) . Maintaining the aesthetic pioneered on the \u2018Volume 1\u2019 mixtape, Ivy Lab continued to garner widespread acclaim with tracks such as \u2018Spooky Dub\u2019, \u2018Can\u2019t Say No\u2019 & \u2018Peninsula\u2019 , supplemented by showpiece remixes for Banks, Noisia, Wilkinson & Wretch 32 - with the era culminating in the 2018 release of their debut album \u201cDeath Don\u2019t Always Taste Good\u201d - the outfits first body of work as a duo - which launched with the critically acclaimed single \u2018Cake\u2019. With an increasingly solid audience in North America and 2 long-play, largely dancefloor oriented projects behind them, the duo have increasingly experimented with more subdued productions; doubling down on the under-produced minimalism that was always a lingering theme of the outfit, but since 2019, has become a touchstone of their productions. Ivy Lab\u2019s currency as bass music figureheads has seen them receive support from such key festivals as Glastonbury, Coachella, EDC Vegas, SXSW, Sonar (Barcelona + HK), CTM Berlin, Dour, ADE, Woo Hah!, Shambhala, Lightning In A Bottle, Lowlands, Origin NYE, Exit and Outlook. Fast forward to COVID-19 pandemic, Ivy Lab took it upon themselves to thrive through the major setbacks that came into place due to borders shutting down and loss of events. Curating virtual streams to be viewed worldwide featuring world-renowned musicians and visual artists, they showcased their art globally only gaining an even larger audience to crave their sounds outside of their hometown in London. As the world returned to its daily life - the duo came back to their US with their first show in over a year at one of the most famous venues in the world, Red Rocks in Colorado. Riding off the success from that show, Ivy Lab continued to tour the states hitting markets such as Los Angeles, New York, all the way to Coachella. Ivy Lab released their album, Infinite Falling Ground, which was paired with an Audio/Visual tour in 2022-2023, & was in consideration for a Grammy Nomination. The duo embarked on their latest journey of club records in early 2024, as well as tapping back into their original roots of Drum & Bass before gearing up for the release of their next album, Infinite Falling Ground Pt. 2. They followed up the album with another Audio/Visual tour in the fall of 2024, hitting cities all across the US and Europe. In 2025, Ivy Lab is kicking the year off with a run of Drum n Bass shows across the United States before they gear up for their next set of club releases."}

Breaking through in the mid-2010s, it was in the latter half of that decade when the Bristol-born artist came into his own, releasing his most successful run of singles to date. As well as a succession of celebrated solo hits, there was also \u2018Whippet\u2019, his inescapable collaboration with Sammy Virji, and \u2018Ladbroke Grove\u2019, a production for AJ Tracey that not only went double platinum in the UK charts, but officially now stands as the best-selling UK garage record in history. As a DJ, Conducta's stock also sky-rocketed, with a packed worldwide diary and a regular schedule of acclaimed DJ mixes, including a contribution to the BBC\u2019s flagship Essential Mix series and his Kiwi Krush mixtape - the latter chosen as Resident Advisor\u2019s number one mix of 2019. Subsequent years would see him star on the cover of both DJ Mag and Mixmag, establishing himself at the top table of UK dance music talent. Of course, Conducta\u2019s story is not complete without mentioning the label he formerly ran, Kiwi Rekords. Launched in 2019, Kiwi not only became synonymous with the cutting edge of modern UK Garage, championing the most exciting talent from the then-burgeoning scene, but also allowed Conducta full control of his own musical narrative and messaging. Although he closed Kiwi in 2024, having completed the label\u2019s mission, it is widely lauded as one of the most important and exciting dance labels of recent times, winning Record Label of the Year at the 2020 DJ Mag awards. Conducta has continued his upward trajectory into 2024, expanding what he does in pretty much every direction and introducing a more diverse musical palette - as exhibited on his genre-spanning \u2018In Transit\u2019 EP, a flagship five-track release that draws from all corners of UK soundsystem culture, and on a recent North American tour which saw him play extended back-to-back sets with both modern club pioneer Swisha and dance music royalty in Todd Edwards. As comfortable performing at New York\u2019s most respected underground spots like Nowadays (which he sold out this last May) and Sustain Release as he is bringing down the house night after night on a sold-out UK tour, Conducta has carved out an incomparable niche - and done it on his own terms."}

With his distinctive songwriting style, high-energy output, and stunning live show, Dimension has received support from every major name in electronic music. Today, the producer and DJ\u2019s style, sound, and attitude have fused into a singular vision that has fueled his rapid rise to global stardom.\n\nDimension\u2019s momentum began with a VIP-packed 2018 Fabriclive mix, followed by his 2021 debut solo album, Organ, which reached the top of the Official UK Dance Chart. His breakthrough was further amplified by two massive collaborations with Sub Focus: the platinum-selling \u201cDesire\u201d (2018) and gold-certified \u201cReady To Fly\u201d (2022).\n\nIn 2023, Dimension hit a new peak: his solo single \u201cDJ Turn It Up\u201d and his remix of MK & Dom Dolla\u2019s \u201cRhyme Dust\u201d became festival anthems and ranked as the second and third highest-selling drum & bass tracks of the year on Beatport. He later remixed Marlon Hoffstadt\u2019s \u201cIt\u2019s That Time,\u201d which became one of the most heavily supported tracks of the year. The milestone year closed with a sold-out headline show at London\u2019s Wembley Arena \u2014 cementing Dimension as one of the few drum & bass artists ever to sell out the iconic venue.\n\nRecently, Dimension joined the WORSHIP tour, performing sold-out shows across North America alongside Sub Focus, Culture Shock, and 1991. The 2024 tour became the biggest drum & bass tour in U.S. history, with performances at Mission Ballroom (Denver), the Hollywood Palladium (LA), and NYC\u2019s Great Hall. He also took the stage at Ultra Miami and EDC Las Vegas. \u201cWe\u2019re drum & bass mercenaries,\u201d Dimension says with a grin.\n\nA defining thread in Dimension\u2019s artistry is his meticulous attention to detail. His live show features state-of-the-art light design and a bespoke, clear-glass instrument built exclusively for him. Blending drum machines, synths, and live MIDI performance, the experience is designed to feel more like a concert than a rave. His original aesthetic direction \u2014 \u201cornate, simple, elegant, powerful\u201d \u2014 defined a visual and sonic identity that stands apart from mass-produced dance music.\n\nIn the studio, that attention to detail is just as pronounced. He writes, produces, mixes, and masters all of his own music, keeping complete creative control. \u201cDrum & bass is competitive from a sound-engineering perspective,\u201d he explains. \u201cMy sweet spot is when a track is incredibly technically engineered but still has real emotion and strong songwriting.\u201d\n\nDimension credits his artistic discipline to Pendulum, whose album Hold Your Colour changed everything for him. Already playing piano and guitar, he discovered Fruity Loops and suddenly found a way to turn ideas into fully formed productions without being limited by playing technique. A YouTube channel promoting underground music eventually led him to Sebastian Weingartshofer. Together they started Regal Records. When Weingartshofer landed an internship at Chase & Status\u2019 More Than Alot (MTA) Records, he showed them Dimension\u2019s music \u2014 and they offered a deal immediately. Dimension describes the moment as life-changing: \u201cHaving their stamp of credibility turned everybody\u2019s heads.\u201d\n\nNow, a decade later, Dimension sits firmly in the global spotlight. April marks the release of \u201cSatellite,\u201d a self-released collaborative single with Alison Wonderland. Following the success of the WORSHIP tours, he\u2019s stepping into international solo dominance. He will be the first international artist to ever play drum & bass on the Tomorrowland mainstage, and will appear across the world\u2019s most influential festivals including Creamfields Asia, Ultra, EDC Vegas, Snowbombing, Love Saves The Day, HARD Summer LA, Beats For Love, Electric Forest, Shambhala, Pukkelpop, and more. Additional tours across Australia and New Zealand are also scheduled.\n\nSeeing a new generation of EDM-raised fans embrace drum & bass \u2014 and witnessing arenas fill for him \u2014 Dimension recognizes a shift. \u201cDrum & bass was not cool for a long time, and sometimes we felt left out of the electronic music discussion,\u201d he says. \u201cBut for the last 10 years we\u2019ve been playing to tens of thousands of people every weekend. Now that drum & bass is in vogue, the audience\u2019s appetite is wild. I\u2019m so excited to show the world our sound.\u201d"}

act = {"start": "2026-05-22 20:00", "end": "2026-05-22 22:00", "stage": "Woogie", "act": "DJ HEARTSTRING", "url": "https://open.spotify.com/artist/5tcwaJBUyEdxQxvieuQxU7?si=dLsGYbhPQvePmJJpWCiULA&nd=1&dlsi=695b540a65934301", "blurb": "Duality has always been key for clubland\u2019s cupids DJ HEARTSTRING. Whether it\u2019s their balance between melancholy and euphoria, the way in which the German duo bring pop bangers to the dancefloor, or their crossover appeal that makes them equally as at home on big festival stages as playing Berghain, producers, DJs and songwriters Leo and Jonas have always played to each other\u2019s strengths.\n\nHowever, long before they became globe-touring artists with tens of millions of streams who can turn a Berlin corner shop into a tiny rave (with the help of pop icons Sugababes), they were two friends making music for fun. Growing up in a small village without a clubbing scene, Leo instead discovered EDM and artists like Deadmau5 by playing the video game DJ Hero and, aged 16, seeing Netsky perform at a festival. Watching everyone there dancing to his music made Leo think it must be the best feeling on earth. Inspired, he asked his parents for a set of turntables and later received Fruity Loops as a Christmas present.\n\nAfter a six-month music production course, Leo moved to Berlin, found its techno scene and was introduced to city native Jonas who, formerly a fan of alternative rock and German hip-hop, was a regular at renowned underground clubs Magdalena and Tresor. Having been introduced to electronic music via Paul Kalkbrenner\u2019s movie \u2018Berlin Calling\u2019, he got into production and was throwing open air parties with friends; alongside one pal, Jonas was booked to DJ a small 18-plus party when they were just 16.\n\nAfter several years of hanging out, it wasn\u2019t until clubs closed in 2020 that Leo and Jonas started messing around making tunes together \u2014 though, crucially, they didn\u2019t put pressure on themselves. Realising they could do everything using just a laptop, they bounced onto the scene in 2021 with their Trance Dance Music (TDM) sound. With a generation of new fans hungry for increased BPMs, the pair \u2014 who came up with their artist moniker after brainstorming the most clich\u00e9, cheesy, trance-sounding names possible \u2014 quickly found their hard-and-fast primed audience. Keeping their faces obscured from social media in the early days also made clear that, while they might not take themselves too seriously, it\u2019s all about the music.\n\nWhen venues reopened, the duo\u2019s euphoric yet emotionally-charged hits and high-energy nostalgia-tinged DJ sets \u2014 which typically feature unreleased tunes, tracks by like-minded artists and a big hands-in-the-air Coldplay moment \u2014 not only made them stand out from the crowd, but proved a tonic for ravers ready to let loose post-pandemic. Leo and Jonas have similarly made up for lost time: in 2024, they played Japan, Europe and America, and went viral with their Boiler Room Melbourne set; this year, they\u2019ll make their Thailand/southeast Asia debut, head to South America for the first time, play a string of festivals and tour North America.\n\nDespite such a packed schedule, artistic evolution remains key for the duo whose next EP, the emotion-filled \u2018You Are The Sun, I Am The Sky\u2019, is the result of the pair locking themselves away in an Airbnb in the German countryside. Doing nothing except making music (and eating frozen pizzas) resulted in a four-track collection of loved-up dancefloor heaters. Ravey opener \u2018Emotion Overload\u2019 not only gets the party popping but truly lives up to the intensity of its name, embodying the duo\u2019s hard trance sound as synths build to a huge earworm hook before the whole thing explodes with untamed elation. \u2018Last Time Under Purple Skies\u2019 is sure to have strangers hugging, eyes-closed, beneath neon strobes, and peak-time pumper \u2018Green Wide Open\u2019 is a surefire bet for this year\u2019s summer anthem thanks to its Ibiza-ready hedonism. Bringing the EP to a close, the comparatively reflective \u2018Stay Awake\u2019 is destined to soundtrack that moment before the club lights come back on \u2014 one last rush before the end of the night.\n\nTo celebrate its release, DJ HEARTSTRING will play their biggest show to date in February: a Valentine\u2019s Day rave at London\u2019s 3,000-capacity Camden Roundhouse that\u2019s likely to get tears falling on the dancefloor, and plenty of calls to ex-partners. Encapsulating the pair\u2019s live, laugh, love vibe perfectly, Jonas has the last word: \u201cwe just want people to feel something!"}
